                   President of the World Peace Unification Family, Hwang Seon-jo

1)
The Lost Sheep and the Father
Matthew 18:1-14
<Prayer> Father, half of this year has already passed. It has been ten years since this nation was invaded by the forces of evil. We have been a pitiful people, filled with worry and anxiety, hoping for tomorrow while living today in distress.
Father, we spend our days wondering what new thing we can present before You today, and while hoping for such tomorrows, we pass our months, and as we hope for those months, we pass our years, caught up in an uncontrollable, frantic pace. You know well that we, who are in such a flow, are struggling to find time to pause our steps and face You, and that we have a desperate desire to return something of our hearts before You.
We are aware of the responsibility to dedicate time to You that others cannot offer, and we have a duty to present the sincerity that others cannot bring before You. Therefore, as time goes on, we each feel an anxious heart and a desperate spirit toward Your will, rather than a heart toward the world.
Father, the days of worrying about tomorrow and today have passed. The day of reckoning is approaching, and the day of settling accounts is also drawing near. We know that heaven is moving us within our living sphere in preparation for those days. Through circumstances, emotions, experiences, or any empirical facts, we clearly understand how we should live and how we should proceed.
Father, the sorrow of six thousand years of providence is great, but we believe that Your heart, looking upon us who are in an environment where we cannot hesitate, is even more pained.
Father, we have understood Your sorrow that cannot feel joy and cannot boast to the world, and we have also recognized Your inner anguish that must expose the historical facts and take revenge on the enemies who have troubled this land. Therefore, Father, whether we live or die, let us be those who step forward solely for You. Whether it rains or snows, whether fierce winds blow, or even if chains and barbed wire lie ahead of us, even if our bones are crushed and our flesh is torn, we hold a heart that will not change our pledge to You, so please believe this.
It is our wish, as descendants of fallen ancestors, to become beings whom You can trust and feel at ease with. We sincerely hope to become sons and daughters whom You can entrust with eternal and noble things and call true. We once again bow before You, vowing to become such sons and daughters. We understand that You are not just the Father of any church or any nation. To become the Father of a nation or a church, we must first go through the process of being our own Father.
Father! Do we truly know Your circumstances? Do we truly regard You as our Father? We have realized that the issue lies here. No matter what anyone says, the tangled circumstances between You and us are greater than anything in the world, yet we have searched for the great things of the world.
We have understood that everything must be resolved by us. We have learned from the words that even Jesus, who came to this earth, longed for His beloved disciples to establish such standards. They were to realize that if they could not bear the responsibilities before heaven, they would become inadequate beings who could not lift their faces. Yet, we know they argued about who was the greatest before Jesus. We understand that they, who should have felt a sense of awe before heaven, asked who would be the greatest in the kingdom of heaven. Today, as we stand in the aftermath of the second millennium, let us be those who do not lose our roots.
Father, even if we could meet the Jesus who felt hunger when hungry, wept when sad, and discussed difficult circumstances with His disciples, we know that there is no one who can meet Him beyond the standards that heaven desires. Even today, after sending Him to heaven, we must comfort Him, knowing His heart and circumstances. We have the responsibility to comfort Him, who walked a sorrowful path on this earth, so allow us to be sons and daughters who can sacrifice everything and not hesitate to walk the path of death if it is something that can bring You joy.
Let us understand that only You know the heights and depths, and let us realize that there are no high or low positions for those who possess You, and that only those who love You deeply will stand in the higher position of sons.
We must become sons and daughters who long for Your embrace, forget everything, and strive to understand Your heart. We hope to live with Your deep heart, love with Your deep heart, and discuss while living with Your deep heart, so that we may be seen as the lowest of the low on the outside but possess heaven and earth.
We have realized that there were no friends of Jesus' sorrowful heart on this earth, and we earnestly ask for the grace to be friends of Jesus' heart even today.
On this day, there are Your sons and daughters in various parts of South Korea, appealing to You with lonely hearts. Please be with them, and bless the many denominations and nations.
Many spirits in heaven are seeking conditions for reconciliation on this earth, so we earnestly ask that we may fulfill all the remaining responsibilities before them. We pray all these things in Your name. Amen.
<Words> The title of the message we wish to reflect on at this time is "The Lost Sheep and the Father." We will speak on the topic of "The Lost Sheep and the Father."
Humans Seeking Worthy Things and God
We know well that every person living on this earth is always searching for something in their hearts. Of course, seeking values that can create a good environment is precious, but we believe that finding oneself, one's own life, and one's own heart, and meeting the owner of that found life and heart, or finding an object of enjoyment, is even more valuable.
Scholars toil and strive to find what they aim for through their studies, but after achieving their goals, what will they do next? Those in power fight tirelessly to gain the power they envision, but what will they do after obtaining that power? Ordinary people are also searching for some valuable thing, but what will they do after finding it? If you find yourselves in such a position, what will you do? This cannot be a trivial matter.
Even if we find ourselves in such a position, we cannot remain satisfied with what we have sought for ourselves alone; it inevitably unfolds into a relationship with others, extending to family, society, nation, world, and even the entire universe. This is a fact that everyone experiences and cannot deny.
Therefore, even if one has a deep desire to exalt only oneself, it cannot be achieved centered solely on oneself. The closer one approaches any standard of value, the more one must be equipped to connect that value to the surrounding environment, the world, and even to the universe. Only then can that value be established as a value for the whole, and only such a person can find happiness. You must understand this.
No matter how accomplished or admirable a person may be, what they possess must be something that everyone desires, and it must be something that all people can feel the value of in a short time. If someone possesses such a value, they will inevitably become a global figure. If that is true for humans, it must also be true for the absolute being who created humans, God.
When God created creatures, there must have been a purpose behind it. It is undeniable that there was a purpose in the process of creating the entire created world, from the smallest individual to the vast universe.
So what is the purpose for which God created humans? We can infer from our lives that God created humans to achieve something known only to Him through them and has been forming relationships with humans ever since.
Today, humans are searching for something. Not only humans but also the absolute being who created humans, God, is searching for something. What are humans looking for? Humans are seeking the most valuable thing. So what is the most valuable thing? If I take myself as an example, it is undoubtedly life. This is something everyone acknowledges and can experience its value in real life. We are searching for the value of life and longing for it. At the same time, we are seeking the value of an object that corresponds to that value of life.
So what happens after finding the value of that object? Once the relative standard is established, it does not remain there but must move and act like the universe. This is an inevitable conclusion. How can we reach this conclusion? It is based on observing physical phenomena. When a relative relationship is established, there must be phenomena of action and movement, and rather than linear movement, there are phenomena of circular movement. We can also conclude this from observing physical phenomena that move to establish relationships with the whole rather than just the individual.
The First Stage of Seeking
So, throughout the historical course, has there been anyone who lived as a being of value that countless people sought, revered, and aimed for? This is the crux of the matter. Moreover, to be called the crown of creation, humans must possess a standard of life that can boast of values greater than those of the universe, yet humans have not equipped themselves with such standards. So what is the purpose of God granting humans the value of being the crown of creation! 
Here we understand that humans are beings searching for the value of life, but creation...
search for the owner. This is the situation we find ourselves in today. 

We must recognize that we are like lost sheep, wandering without knowing our true owner. We have to understand that the true owner is not just a distant figure but is intimately connected to our lives, our values, and our purpose. 

In this state of confusion and uncertainty, we must strive to find our true purpose and the true owner of our lives. Only then can we hope to escape the despair and emptiness that comes from being lost. 

The path to finding our true owner is not an easy one. It requires a deep understanding of our own hearts and a commitment to seek out the divine connection that exists between us and God. 

As we embark on this journey, we must be aware of the dangers that lie ahead. The world around us may seem comforting, but it can also be filled with distractions and false promises. We must remain vigilant and focused on our quest for truth and meaning. 

In conclusion, the search for our true owner, our true purpose, and our true values is a journey that each of us must undertake. It is a journey that requires courage, determination, and a willingness to confront the challenges that lie ahead. Only by doing so can we hope to find the fulfillment and happiness that we seek.
We must run. Not only must we run, but we must cry out with all our strength. This is the secret to finding the Master. We must drink the water we used to drink and eat the grass we used to eat, but if the Master sleeps carelessly whether He is present or not, He will surely become the food for wolves or lions.

The true path of virtue is one that must be taken by breaking away from the world. Jesus came to this earth as the Lamb. John the Baptist cried out to behold the Lamb of God who takes away the sin of the world. So, what kind of Lamb did Jesus come as? He came as the Lamb to show the way. He did not come as a lost lamb but as a lamb that knows where the Master is. Therefore, Jesus said to abandon your family. He did not say to fulfill your responsibilities there because it is good. He did not say to fulfill your responsibilities in the country you live in or in the church you believe in because they are good.

This land is the land of enemies. The Master is different. The original Master who gave birth to me and raised me does not know how to value all the vital elements of my life. He does not value them. However, the enemy demands compensation for everything I eat, wear, and sleep on, and eventually even demands compensation for life itself. Because of this life, God has dealt with humanity in a contradictory, paradoxical, and speculative manner until now, and from that perspective, He has governed history.

Therefore, we must be cautious of enemies. At the same time, we must know the secrets of the enemies. We must know the paths the enemies come from and where the enemies are. If we know the secrets, there is a way to avoid them. However, if we do not know the secrets, there is no way to escape. If we just sleep comfortably and live carelessly, we will lose even our lives. This is the state of humanity living on this earth. It is the same whether one is successful or not.

Thus, God has warned humanity. He has warned us. Did He say to cling to the world? No. He said to break away from the world. Isn't that what must be done? That is how one becomes the true Master. If one simply tells humanity that they should live well after seeing the lost Master, that is the enemy.

Therefore, the path of virtue is a path that must be taken by breaking away. It must be done. God desires that humanity, who has lost the Master and does not know the connection to the Master, break away, but humanity is unable to do so. Why? Because they do not know the way. They must go, but they do not know how to go. Do you rely on the theories of some philosopher for your life? Do you rely on some ideology or thought for your life? Are you at ease? You cannot be at ease. Because those are not absolute.

Any philosophy or ideology up to today may have been suitable for a certain era, but it was not suitable for eternal life and the world of the heart. Those were ultimately not things we could believe in and rest upon. Therefore, humanity is like a pitiful traveler. They are in such a position. A traveler must always compensate for their eating and sleeping. The Master can freely move their dwelling and eat and drink as they please, but a traveler cannot do so. They must compensate. They must repay. They must compensate for the food they eat, the water they drink, and the place they sleep.

So what is it that humanity looks forward to and hopes for? A world where they can welcome the true Master of life and where their lives can be joyful, a world where they can take in infinite nutrients and elements of happiness without being demanded compensation. That world, where no compensation is demanded, is truly a happy world. Because God knows well the circumstances of humanity that has lost such a world, He did not say to come together with the world. He said to turn away from the world.

The meaning of the way, the truth, and the life that Jesus spoke of. Jesus came to this earth 2,000 years ago. What kind of life did Jesus live? What did He bring before the pitiful humans, who were like orphans or beggars, or even more pitiful humans who wanted to receive compensation after receiving? Jesus said, "I am the way, the truth, and the life." Is that really true? Is it really so?

Then what kind of way is that? It is not an ordinary way; it is one way, a way without forgiveness. If there is one way that all beings desire, what kind of way is it? There is only one way to live and die. To live and die means to conclude life. What kind of way did Jesus claim and walk? It is the way of living without dying. It is the way of living if you go and dying if you do not go. It is the way that determines life and death. You should not seek the way to live well by accumulating money, but rather seek the way that determines life and death.

Next, what is that truth? The one who belongs to that truth is the truth that can surpass compensation. The one who belongs to that truth can overcome the issue of compensation in all matters of eating, wearing, and sleeping. Therefore, the early Christian believers who knew Jesus transcended the issues of eating and wearing.

Then what kind of life is the life Jesus spoke of? The life Jesus spoke of is a life that has the authority to even move God. Having the authority of life means containing love. It means containing a life that God cannot help but love. That is the life He spoke of. Therefore, Jesus said, "I am the way, the truth, and the life; no one comes to the Father except through me." (John 14:6)

Then what should we, who follow Jesus, have? We must have the way. We must have the truth. We must have the life. Christianity was established to give the way, truth, and life to the lost lambs so they can return. You, who are centered on that ideology, must first stand on a standard that can transcend material concepts. You must be able to transcend the concepts of eating, wearing, and sleeping. If you do not have the ability to transcend that, you cannot endure in this world.

Next, centered on the name of Jesus, we must not have death as a problem. We must be able to overcome the fear of death. This is how believers in Jesus should be. Whether you die in ten years or fifty years, dying is the same. If you are one who sings of eternal life, what does it matter if you die in a thousand years or a year? We must be able to overcome the peak of death.

In the Bible, Jesus said, "I am the way, the truth, and the life; no one comes to the Father except through me," and I believe that love must be included there. If I were to say it, I would say, "I am the way, the truth, the life, and love." Of course, the center of Jesus is love. This love is established after one has walked the entire way.

Those who believe in Jesus should not shed tears when things do not go well. A believer should not say, "Oh! I cannot live like this." Even if the danger of life approaches, they should have the conviction to overcome the power of death. The historical turmoil of this land has also been due to issues of a static nature. Therefore, we must also revolutionize static issues. Even in situations where dozens fall, if you think that you will fall within your will, you can boldly overcome. You must have this kind of spirit. Jesus was like that.

However, from the perspective of those who find joy in the world, from the standpoint of humans who see, feel, and enjoy happiness, Jesus was a pitiful figure. Joseph and Mary did not know when they would give birth and went to find their hometown, ultimately giving birth to Jesus in a stable. After that, do you think Jesus lived well? Absolutely not. Jesus grew up as a stepson. As Joseph's stepson, do you think Joseph treated Jesus as the Son of God? No. Jesus grew up as Joseph's stepson. 

From the moment He was born, He had to walk the path of suffering, but Jesus remained silent. For some reason, an angel appeared to Him in a dream and said He was the Son of God, and He believed it, but after giving birth, they forgot everything. When the wise men from the East came and offered gifts, they eventually forgot everything and lived a normal life every day. We must understand that Jesus lived swept away in the family life of Joseph and Mary.

The time of testimony is one time, but the time of hope when the testimony is fulfilled comes only after a certain period. However, even the wise men who testified about Jesus all left, and Anna and the shepherds all left. Even John the Baptist, who was older, testified at first but later opposed Him.

The family of Joseph did not like Jesus, who brought the ideals of heaven. His siblings, sisters, and brothers all disliked Him. Do you think Jesus fought or did anything like that while growing up? He was silent. He remained quiet. His eyes wanted to see something else, His ears wanted to hear something else, and His mouth wanted to speak different words. He wanted to feel something different.

Jesus grew up pitifully in the family of Joseph. Nothing matched. How desperate must He have been to leave home at the age of twelve? When He went up to the temple in Jerusalem alone to argue with the priests, His parents did not look for Him. Just think about it. Of course, there must have been a mission of purpose, but from a human perspective, how desperate must He have been to leave home at the age of twelve? What must have been in Jesus' heart?

At the moment He was crucified, Jesus could have expressed all the emotions of His thirty years of life, but He did not speak. What must have been in the heart of Jesus, who had to leave home as a boy? He was a pitiful Jesus. The Bible does not record such things. It says that during the holidays, He wanted to eat delicious food. He wanted to wear fine clothes and beautiful garments. But Jesus remained silent. He was treated carelessly. He served His stepfather, a carpenter, and lived quietly while planing wood.

It is time for a correct understanding of Jesus. Jesus was not the one you are believing in today, saying, "Oh! Lord." If those who believe well today had been born back then, they would not have believed Him if He had said, "This man is your Lord." Not a single person would have believed. Historically, when they are told to place the value of Jesus on a global standard, they believe.

Do you think the priests of old killed Jesus because they were inferior to you? Absolutely not. Jesus was in a deplorable position, whether viewed by lineage or anything else. After Jesus died, the Bible says that His lineage was great, so people believed that, but what did the people of that time know? Whether looking at the past or the present, there was nothing to believe in Jesus. Therefore, even His siblings spoke ill of Him. When it came time for Pentecost or any event, if the older brother wanted to show something, they would scold Him for not going to Jerusalem, where people gathered.

During His public ministry, even while performing miracles and signs by the power of God, Jesus suffered. People looked down on Him, saying, "Isn't that the brother of someone?" He was in a poor position.

For over thirty years, Jesus prepared His life and had something He desperately wanted to say to His mother. He had something He wanted to say to His brothers. However, Jesus could not speak. Why? Because the standard of the counterpart was not established. Jesus, knowing that He could not break away from the entangled feelings with His parents, Joseph and Mary, and His growing siblings, broke away from home when He turned thirty.

You know that Jesus came out to preach the gospel, right? That is absolutely wrong. Did He come out to save all mankind? Why could Jesus not evangelize centered around the family of Joseph and His relatives? If His relatives had been His supporters, He would not have died. However, that situation did not exist.

Because Jesus broke away from home, when Mary appeared at the wedding in Cana and told Him that there was no wine, He said to Mary, "Woman, what does that have to do with me?" It is only natural. It is fortunate that He did not slap her. I see it that way. Who would understand that feeling? As the circumstances became entangled and the heart felt like it was being torn apart, the more earnest the heart was toward the heavenly principle, the more the anxiety and unease increased as the time drew near.

People living on this earth become anxious and uneasy because they do not know the way, but you must understand that Jesus was anxious and uneasy because He could not teach humanity the way they should go.

You must think about it. The Pharisees, the Jews, and the Israelite people had been prepared for four thousand years. For four thousand years, God taught them the law through providence. He had them build the temple so that they could receive and welcome the Messiah when He came. Yet, Peter became the disciple of Jesus? That is frustrating. What about Peter? Peter was a fisherman. Even today, in Korea, if someone is a fisherman, they are thought of poorly, and yet that person became a disciple of Jesus? A foolish fisherman became a disciple of Jesus?

The King of Kings, the only begotten Son of God, came to this earth and chose a fisherman named Peter as His disciple? Think about it. Those who were excellent and capable of leading that era should have said, "I will follow you whether I die or live if you command." But there were no such people. There were people like that, but He chose a fisherman as a disciple? Absolutely not.

Therefore, Jesus was thoroughly separated. He became a Jesus who fell into a pitiful position. The unwise priests did not ask Jesus, "Are you the Messiah?" Not a single one. Look at the Bible. Did they or did they not? No Pharisee or priest, nor anyone with the status of a scribe became one of Jesus' twelve disciples.

Jesus was surrounded by the representatives of the Israelite people, surrounded by the scribes, and surrounded by the priests. So where would He go? Would He go to the mountains because He liked the mountains and prayed all night?

You must overturn everything you have believed until now. Even if there is nowhere to go, Jesus was determined to fulfill His purpose. He felt a sense of mission that He must establish even a poor existence to fulfill His purpose on earth, and because of that earnest feeling, He had no choice but to seek out a fisherman.

When Jesus said, "Peter, leave everything and follow me," do you think Peter said, "Yes," and followed Him? Absolutely not. Peter saw and understood everything that was happening to Jesus. The Bible says that when Jesus called out to Peter, it seems like Peter followed by the power of the Son of God, but that is not the case. They were fishermen who were despised by all the scribes of Israel. Therefore, they had resentment against the scribes and the leaders who ruled that era.

When they saw Jesus crying out purely in the form of justice to establish the path of righteousness, they knew He was undoubtedly a good person, but because the scribes hated and pursued Him, they could not help but follow Him. The people who were being pursued began to follow Jesus. The current situation in Korea is similar.
Doesn't it? The same goes for this. It's the same.
Everyone, look. How much did Jesus suffer for three years while carrying around ignorant disciples? How desperate must He have been to wash the feet of His disciples? Did He do it because He liked it? No. It turns out to be a heartbreaking fact.
This left Him with nowhere to go. In the end, during the three years of public ministry, when all twelve apostles, who swore to share joy and sorrow and even death, rejected Him, where could He go? Thus, He had no choice but to go the way of the cross. Was there any other way to go? Knowing that such a day would not be far off, Jesus went to the Garden of Gethsemane and prayed, 
"My Father, if it is possible, let this cup pass from me; nevertheless, not as I will, but as you will." (Matthew 26:39) But the situation was already dire. That is why Jesus died on the cross.
The Purpose and Desire of Jesus' Coming
So what was the purpose of Jesus coming to this earth? He came to introduce the true way to the lost sheep and the people wandering in the wilderness, as well as to all of humanity. He was the only begotten Son sent by God for this purpose, but the path He took was a miserable one.
Since Jesus did not speak about how He lived His life for over 30 years, there is no content about that in the Bible. He did not tell the disciples what kind of path He walked, what sorrows He felt, how He was treated by His parents, or the trials He faced with His siblings. He had many deep feelings in His heart, but He did not say a word. What was in Jesus' journey? He had nothing to boast about, which is why He could not speak.
"Disciples, you should follow the example of my Father, you should follow the example of my mother, you should follow the example of my siblings." He could not say this because there were no conditions to say so.
The life of Jesus, who grew up in the household of Joseph for 30 years, was a life of regret and sighs. In such a life, Jesus, who was constantly pressured and ultimately rejected even by His believing disciples, could only think of death, which is why He went to the Garden of Gethsemane.
Did Jesus have to die to save all people? Is it true that without dying, He could not save anyone? Then when Jesus said, 
"I am the way, the truth, and the life; no one comes to the Father except through me." (John 14:6) was it after He was crucified or before? When was it? It was before. Most of the words found in the four Gospels were spoken before He died on the cross. It was not when He was being pressured and about to die. How wonderful it would have been if He had been acknowledged as the Savior while He was alive!
God is surely one who sends a true shepherd to those who are wandering like lost sheep, to those who have lost their sense of purpose and the value of life. That is why He sent the only begotten Son, establishing the name of the Savior through the prophets, to send His Son to this earth. Centered around Him, Christianity emerged as a historical new movement.
So what did Jesus seek to achieve through His 30 years of life? It was to create glorious sons and daughters who transcended the standards of life and death through God's heart and God's life, and to set them before all the world. That was what Jesus sincerely desired. However, that hope was completely shattered.
Jesus left without being able to say what He wanted to say. Where in the Bible is it written that Jesus said everything He wanted to say? 
"I have much to say to you, but you cannot bear it now. However, when the Spirit of truth comes, He will guide you into all truth." He said. Jesus left without being able to say what He wanted to say.
Jesus, who came as a shepherd to humanity, had the responsibility to teach the way to find God, the way to find the Master, but He could not teach it to anyone on earth. Have you thought about the heart of Jesus? Therefore, we must pray. If we do not pray, we must be made to pray.
Then what is the purpose of prayer? Jesus opened the standard by saying, "I am the way, the truth, the life, and love," but has anyone walked that path? No. Not even in Christianity.
That is why there must be a new movement that can strike at the reality of this situation. We must burn away the historical masks and awaken a new heart to fulfill the mission of this era, the mission toward humanity and the world. There must be a group that acts to achieve such a world of that way, that life, that truth, and that love, which is undoubtedly the hope of heaven's providence.
