We must live like that. Even if we die, we must die with such a heart. We must fight against Satan. And then we must be able to say, "Father, I have fought against Satan and won." Only then can we go to heaven and subdue Satan to pass judgment. We must go with this standard.

Those who want to eat well, dress well, and live well, do not follow this path. The path we are taking is the path that pierces through the depths of hell. If you love your children more, live well with them. If you love your spouse more, live well with them. If you feel your parents are more precious, live well with them.

God is in a position to demand restitution and compensation from us, but He does not demand any restitution or compensation from us. Therefore, we must have the loyalty of a faithful servant, the loyalty of a filial son, and the loyalty of a virtuous woman before God. 

If we have started with such loyalty, we must go even if it means falling and dying. We must march forward to find our lost original Father.

<Prayer> Father, there are many people living on the earth and many nations, but I have realized that there is no one you can trust. I have understood that history has flowed around the oppressed and that the world has been created around them. Now, we who are in the fate of having to return, we who have lost our way, must find our parents' knees, find our brothers' ties, and find our people's ties to re-establish the relationship between Father and son. 

Please allow us to be those who endure until the last day when we can relieve God's resentment, relieve Jesus' resentment, and relieve the resentment of history. 

Through all the grace granted today, please establish a life-giving promise and life-giving covenant with the Father, and do not let us be mocked before the arch-enemy Satan.

I pray all these things in the name of the Lord. Amen. 

2) 

Jesus, Who is Troubled and Distressed

Matthew 21:12-22, 26:36-46, Luke 12:49-53

<Prayer> Father, we are a group that has sworn in our hearts to walk with you in any environment for the rest of our lives. Please look upon your children gathered here and do not let a single life fall from your grasp. Let us be sons and daughters who can go to the place you have permitted, the place you have blessed, fulfilling all that we have resolved and sworn to do before heaven. We earnestly hope and desire this.

Father, as I stand at the altar, please be with me. Now we must learn and resemble the image of Jesus Christ, who came with the heart of God. The Bible tells us that Jesus, who lived on this earth with the Word, indeed walked a pitiful life.

However, we have understood that Jesus, who came with the heavenly connection that all humanity must rely on, was the one responsible for this earth, and that what He wanted to establish on this earth was only the heart of the Father. We understand that His tears were a substitute for the heart of the heavenly Father, and that His hunger was not for His own sake but for the Father’s sake.

As we look toward the last hour of His life, we realize that when Jesus' steps came to rest in the Garden of Gethsemane with a solemn determination and a burning heart, heaven and earth were filled with sorrow, and even the smallest creatures understood Jesus' heart. Yet, we know that humans, who should have fulfilled their responsibilities and become the protagonists of all creation, could not empathize with Jesus' heart and thus could not share in His sorrow.

We must remind ourselves of the unjust fact that we treated the Messiah, who came with the heart of God, in such a way that we severed the heavenly connection. At this time, let us recall the scene of the disciples sleeping in the Garden of Gethsemane two thousand years ago and think about what kind of figures we would become if we stood in such a position, so that we can make new resolutions and determinations. 

Furthermore, we hope that this grace will dwell deeply in our hearts.

At this time, whatever words are spoken, may you be present with us, and may hearts connect with hearts and minds connect with minds. 

As we are in a process moving toward one purpose, may we be able to move our hearts toward one relationship and one purpose, and may we be able to make new resolutions and new determinations before the heart of the Father through the words spoken. 

May the heart of the speaker and the heart of the listener become one, and may you move only according to the will of the Father. At this time, may you be with the countless sons and daughters who are kneeling alone and worshiping before the Father. I earnestly hope that you will extend a uniform hand of blessing to them as well, and I entrust this time to you, so please take charge of it. I pray in the name of the Lord. Amen. 

<Message> Today, I will speak on the topic of "Jesus, Who is Troubled and Distressed."

The Unfortunate Beginning of Human History

Among the many people living on the earth, countless individuals know that God exists. They may not know exactly who God is, but in their hearts, everyone acknowledges that God exists. Among them, believers firmly believe that God exists. They believe that all creation comes from God and that the entire history of humanity moves toward a world of purpose according to God's providence. 

Moreover, they believe that God has a direct connection with humanity, and furthermore, with me, and that He has always been in a place of joy until now.
This means that in God's heart, there is no pain, worry, or sorrow.  
However, from the day humanity fell, God has harbored resentment towards humanity. A God with true love cannot abandon the principles and ideals through which He created humanity and governed them, which is why He cannot help but feel resentment towards humanity. Therefore, God lamented over the creation of man and was troubled in His heart.  
When we ask whether human history began with happiness or unhappiness, no one would say it began with happiness. This is a historically proven fact. Moreover, when we see the physical and mental hardships faced by individuals, we cannot deny that our human ancestors did not start on the path of happiness but rather on the path of unhappiness.  
Today, humans claim to be the masters of all creation. However, when we ask whether those who claim to be the masters of all creation are truly living joyfully as such, no one can affirm that they are.  
When all things created by God are to be under human dominion, if they have a desire, what would that be? In other words, what kind of protagonist would all things want to meet? They would want to meet a protagonist who is infinitely happy, infinitely free, and infinitely glorious. All things are longing for a protagonist who can embrace them. However, the humans living on this earth have started from a place centered around the noun "unhappiness," not the nouns "happiness," "freedom," or "peace." For this reason, no matter how much someone boasts, they must realize that when they appear before all things, they are in a shameful position that must prove their own shortcomings.  
First, we must understand that we are shameful beings who cannot stand before the heavenly principle that God intended to elevate us as representatives of all things. Furthermore, we must acknowledge that there is God's earnest heart that wants to boast of us before all creation by forming a heartfelt connection with us.  
God, who does not reveal His own sorrow  
Although humanity, which started in unhappiness, should end in unhappiness, God, who must lead such humanity to a place of happiness, cannot be happy Himself. And God, who has not been able to lead humanity out of such an unhappy position for thousands of years until today, must undoubtedly feel infinite pain.  
The unhappiness, or pain and sorrow, that an individual feels is personal unhappiness and personal sorrow.  
Through a long history, God has led humanity to the garden of happiness. However, He has not yet fulfilled that purpose. It is an inevitable fact that humanity cannot be happy unless God leads them out of the place of suffering. Because God bears such responsibility, He feels unhappiness more deeply than anyone else, and He experiences pain and sorrow more intensely than anyone else, and He cannot escape from that situation.  
Until now, many people who have sought the way of virtue and followed God's commands have called out in times of suffering:  
"God, please bear this suffering."  
In times of sorrow, they have said to Heaven, "Please take this sorrow upon Yourself and move me to a place of peace." Many religious people have done this until now.  
If God is in such a position, He must truly be a pitiful being. However, while He possesses a pitiful situation, a pitiful heart, and a pitiful mind, He does not want to show His pitiful appearance before fallen humanity, nor does He wish to reveal His own sorrow before them.  
Why? Because this world is governed by Satan. God does not want to show His miserable state before Satan. Therefore, until today, God has been providentially working without revealing His pain and miserable circumstances to the countless people under Satan's dominion. This is a fact we can infer. We must understand that God is like this.  
Now, when you have a sincere desire and pray before the Father, you must recognize that you are praying before a God who is in such a painful and miserable position. Also, whenever you have a desire and move according to His will, you must think about the responsibility you bear before Heaven.  
If there was someone among the many prophets and sages who came and went in the course of history who understood that they were praying before such a God and were burning with a sense of duty to fulfill the responsibilities and missions they bore, even if their nation betrayed and slandered them, they would not have betrayed Heaven. However, the prophets of the past often forgot the time and circumstances and betrayed Heaven.  
What is the motivation and cause of this? It lies in the belief that God is always in a joyful position and must fulfill all our wishes. Because of this, we must recognize that the prophets have betrayed Heaven and gone against the heavenly path.  
If our ancestors had known that Heaven was more pitiful than they were, more unjust than they were, more lonely than they were, and more painful than they were, and if they had lived with that sentiment, they would not have even considered the words betrayal or rejection. However, the prophets of the past did not know this fact. They only knew God as the source of happiness and peace. Thus, they left behind such historical blemishes. Through these facts, we must once again contemplate God's heart.  
Today, we who have gathered here have spoken of God's circumstances. We have spoken of God's will. We have also learned and understood what God's will is, what God's circumstances are, and what God's heart is like. Now is the time to protest against our ancestors who did not know God's heart and circumstances. Knowing God's circumstances, we must be burning with a sense of duty to raise a new beacon before humanity, which is walking the opposite path from God.  
The mission of Jesus Christ  
Now is the time to recall the figure of Jesus Christ, who has borne the entire historical course. When God sent His only begotten Son to save all people, why did He not send Him to the royal family of Judea or the house of the high priest? From the perspective of His will, God must have wanted to place Jesus in such a position. But why did He not establish Him in such an environment? Because there was something that had to be established on this earth before Jesus could become the Savior of all people.  
What is that? It is to introduce God's sorrow to humanity. This was Jesus' mission. We must understand that Jesus came to this earth, carrying God's loneliness and hardships, to convey the loneliness and hardships of God that had not been communicated to humanity for 4,000 years.  
What was God's purpose in choosing the Israelite people, promising to send the Messiah, and sending many prophets over 4,000 years to prepare for the coming of the Messiah? It was to create an environment through which Jesus could convey God's heart when He came with God's heart, and furthermore, to find and establish a group that could discuss and fight for God with the same heart while living with that heart. However, when Jesus actually came to the earth, was there a group that could understand Jesus' circumstances and heart? There was none. Were there priests who devoted themselves to God? Were there true Israelites? The more they held a heavenly heart, the more they understood the affairs of the world, and the more they felt the responsibility of carrying the heavenly principle within themselves, the more they must have realized that they had to represent God.  
God, who could not convey His heart to the chosen Israelite people, sent a representative who could convey His heart after 4,000 years, and that representative was none other than Jesus, the Messiah.  
Therefore, the Israelite people who awaited the Messiah should have gone to Jesus and collectively appealed and demanded, "Jesus, what is the heart of God that you have deeply felt? What is God's situation, and what is God's will?" Yet, instead, they often opposed Jesus.  
The disbelief of the Israelite people and the tragic life of Jesus  
God, who established the Israelite people and worked for 4,000 years, sent Jesus to lead the Israelite people, who were not trustworthy, with a heart willing to believe in Him. The Israelite people were those who believed in God and claimed to be loyal to Him, but they did not become a people worthy of trust. This sorrow has reached us even today, and we must not fail to feel it deeply.  
Although Jesus came with God's heart and circumstances, from the day He was born, He did not have the environment to speak of the heart and circumstances of Heaven and fulfill His will.  
God wanted to embrace humanity and speak of His circumstances and heart from a place of freedom. He wanted to bless humanity before all creation from a place of freedom. That was God's desire. However, for 4,000 years, God, who chose and governed the Israelite people, never appeared freely before that people or spoke freely of all heavenly secrets.  
Considering this, we must understand that God had countless hardships regarding humanity, but He could not express all those hardships from beginning to end. Therefore, God sent Jesus to resolve the sorrow of His 4,000 years of providence for salvation and to untangle all the sorrows of history that arose from humanity's betrayal of Heaven. God wanted to resolve all the sorrowful circumstances through Jesus alone. If Jesus had been in a position to share the heavenly circumstances with the Israelite people, they would not have become a people scattered throughout the world.  
Jesus, who had to come to this earth while holding the entire heavenly connection, lived a tragic life for over 30 years. From beginning to end, it was a thoroughly tragic life. As time passed, His heart toward Heaven grew thicker, and the more He understood the affairs of the earth and Heaven, the more He could not forget God's heart for a single moment, nor could He forget the circumstances and will of the Father for even a moment.  
Dear friends, did Jesus ever act freely on this earth? Did He ever say, "I am the Son of God"? Even in Joseph's household, He could not live freely. He could not live a happy life. He could not live a joyful life. Because of the environment, the people He encountered, and the national circumstances, Jesus Himself wanted to be infinitely free in His heart and wanted to lead all humanity in infinite glory and grace before God, but He could not do so.  
Although Jesus came as the true person representing God, He, too, as a human, knew sorrow, knew loneliness, and felt pain. If we exclude God's will, Jesus would have had human emotions and human desires. However, from the day He held God within Him, He disregarded His own will, feelings, and all circumstances, and he had made a solemn resolution that he must dedicate his life to holding onto the responsibilities he bore, God's will, God's circumstances, and God's heart, regardless of what the world said. When God looked at such a figure of Jesus, we must understand how God's heart must have felt. Jesus was infinitely pitiful.  
When Jesus came to this earth to fulfill His will, He made a solemn resolution before the people. Once He started, He made a solemn resolution that there would be no retreat, even if the path of death blocked His way. He was prepared to face death.  
The desires of Jesus, the desires of God  
Among the biblical passages we read today, one thing you must understand is that Jesus was hungry. Jesus was the Savior of all people, the embodiment of the desires that the chosen people had longed for over 4,000 years, and He came with the heavenly circumstances and heavenly heart. Therefore, as long as He is not pleased, no being on this earth can be pleased, and as long as He is not happy, no one on this earth can be happy, and no one on this earth can receive glory until He receives glory.  
Nevertheless, the people of that era wished to be happy before He was pleased and longed to enjoy the glory before He received it. The rulers who moved the times before Jesus had power over Him.  
Heaven is seeking a true day of freedom. It is coming forth to establish and boast of a true person. It is coming forth to create a true person who can receive the greatest glory since the beginning of history. It is coming forth to establish a true person who can govern the entire universe. Shouldn't it be so?  
Before that true person exercises sovereignty, anyone who acts before Him is a traitor. Anyone who stands in the place of glory before He is pleased will be met by Heaven at any time. This is because freedom, peace, happiness, and ideals begin from Heaven. They do not begin from humanity; they begin from God. They do not begin from evil Satan; they begin from good God.  
If there is something Jesus longed for and desired in His heart, what would that be? He longed for and desired freedom centered on God. He hoped for happiness centered on God, peace centered on God, and a world of sovereignty centered on God. Shouldn't it be so?  
However, from the day history began until today, thousands of years have passed, but has there been a historical figure who God looked at and said, "Indeed, you are the king of freedom. You are worthy to live with my ideal of freedom, worthy to live with the ideals of happiness and goodness, and you are someone whom the entire universe can rejoice in"? There has been none.  
If God has a desire, unless a protagonist appears who can fulfill that desire, unless a protagonist appears who can represent God's circumstances, and unless a protagonist appears who can represent God's heart, humanity cannot be happy. If such a protagonist does not appear, even if one claims to be happy, that happiness is not the happiness that God can acknowledge, and even if this earth seems peaceful, it is not the true peace that God can acknowledge.
Who knew such a thing? Did the people of Israel, who were anticipating the Messiah, know? No. The high priests who were preparing to receive the Messiah did not know, nor did the scribes who were leading the Jews. The only one who knew this fact was Jesus, just Jesus. Only the Messiah knew.

Then what is the inherent freedom, hope, circumstances, and heart that we should feel? To understand this, we must study the Bible. Until we understand this, we cannot comprehend the character of Jesus and the emotions of His life. Where did the hope and heart that God was trying to establish go? Today, Christianity boasts of countless believers, but what Christians around the world need to realize is that this earth is still in the process of pioneering a world of peace; it has not yet become a peaceful place recognized by heaven and earth, and we have not yet welcomed the One.

No matter how many teachings or ideologies exist on this earth, they are merely fulfilling the role of a staff in the process.

Now we have come to understand that God also experiences suffering. We have come to know that God has sorrows greater than those of humans. We have learned that God carried the cross and led humanity. Surely, God is looking forward to the day when He can be free. It is unquestionable that God desires to embrace all people in the garden of happiness. Just as God longs for a garden of freedom through which He can communicate His wishes, so too do those who follow God.

The poor Messiah, Jesus. God comes down to find the earth, and humans ascend to seek God. The one who came to connect these two is the Messiah. He is the Savior.

If such a person had not appeared in the course of history, the restoration history would still be far off. Yet, thankfully, although the time and season have passed, Jesus came to the earth as the Son of God, representing humanity on earth, 2,000 years ago. It is truly a grateful thing. In His heart, there must have been a world of peace. In His mind, the idea of freedom must have sprouted. He must have had the content to resolve all human circumstances and a connection to God's heart.

But have you ever heard the joyful song of freedom that God calls for since Jesus left? Have you heard that Jesus danced with joy? Jesus said, "O heaven, O earth, O all creation, rejoice with me." Have you ever done that? In the past, figures like King David or King Solomon would recite poetry when they stood in glory. However, Jesus could not do so. That does not mean that Jesus lacked poetic sentiment or emotion. If He were to sing, He would have to sing a sad song, and if He were to speak, He would have to speak sad words. How pitiful was the Messiah! Is that not so?

Jesus, feeling frustrated and embarrassed, entered the Jerusalem temple with the mission of spreading the Gospel and overturned the tables. Would He have done that out of joy? If the people of Israel had believed in Jesus, and opened the idea of freedom that was deep in His heart, this land would not be as it is today.

We must understand that Jesus was the ultimate idealist. He was the ultimate ideologist. No ideology or thought can surpass Jesus' ideology and thought. If He had rejoiced, then all who connected with that ideology and thought could have rejoiced as well.

Yet Jesus was sorrowful from birth. We must understand this. What does it mean that Jesus' clothes were ragged? If someone had offered Jesus the best food better than anything the people of Israel had ever eaten, or if He had been given more glory than the countless kings who enjoyed glory and splendor for 4,000 years, would God have punished the people of Israel?

Jesus was the King of Kings. And Jesus brought an ideology that no one else had. He brought feelings and circumstances that no one else possessed. He brought not only human circumstances and human feelings and human ideologies but also God's feelings, God's circumstances, and God's wishes. How grateful is that?

Jesus came and prayed. Look at the Bible. Jesus wept. He went to a lonely place and wept. When Jesus was lonely, He went to a quiet mountain. If the people of Israel had believed in Jesus and become one with Him, from that day on, Jesus would have done what He wanted. He had all the plans and methods to implement them. However, He could not put that plan into action. You must remember this. The Messiah sent by heaven to lead the nation and to pioneer the world was so pitiful.

Today, believers think of Jesus as one who came to die. But that is not true. No. Jesus came to speak of God's work, to speak of God's circumstances, to speak of the nation's destiny, and to guide the nation's path. Yet the entire nation rejected Him. Did they not? They rejected Him everywhere He went. This was the appearance of the Savior who came for all people. And it is not just that. Jesus wore clothes that were no better than yours, and He ate no better than you.

As Jesus embarked on His three-year public ministry, He made a solemn resolution. Jesus knew that the path before Him was one of suffering, not glory. He was sent to a place where He could receive infinite glory and blessings, yet He felt that He had to go to a place opposite to glory. We must understand how Jesus felt in such a situation.

He wanted to gather the people of Israel with a heart of glory, but He intended to guide the people of Israel through God's freedom and God's ideology, to embrace Israel in God's arms. He set out with such a heart, but when the nation rejected Him, He had no choice but to go the opposite way. Thus, Jesus had to walk the path of the cross, not the path of glory. Jesus, who should have gone to a flat land, had to cross the rugged peaks of a mountain without a road. The path that God had paved for 4,000 years, the path that Israel had paved, disappeared. When the chosen Israel pushed Jesus away, where did He go? Where did He go? He was chased and pursued, and we must understand that He had to go to Golgotha, prepared for death, crossing the Garden of Gethsemane. How could He speak of freedom and peace when He was in such a pitiful position, being chased and pursued? He could not.

Jesus, who was filial to God and loved the nation. Even if the Messiah were to eat the food offered with sincere hearts by all people, heaven would still feel it was insufficient, so what does it mean for the Messiah to be hungry? We must understand that Jesus was hungry. Jesus, who raised the banner of the Gospel, also had the desire to eat, to wear, and to be at peace, just like us.

Today, believers think that since Jesus is the Son of God, He must have had no problem with a 40-day fast. But that is a huge misconception. The Messiah also feels hunger if He does not eat. However, Jesus did not show signs of hunger. Why did He have to do that? You, being fallen descendants, can fast without affecting the providence, but Jesus, having the dignity of God, could not act carelessly. The King of Kings, who represented 4,000 years of human history, the Prince of Heaven, the only begotten Son of Heaven, had God's dignity in His heart.

No matter how ragged His clothes were, He said, "Father, have patience." He said, "You walked this path, so how can I not walk it?" Every time He felt hungry, He prayed, "Father, I know that You guided the ancestors while walking this path. As Your son, I follow in Your footsteps, so please bear with me." Because of this, the people of Israel at that time were able to avoid being cursed.

Jesus, who should have gathered all people in joy and celebrated in a joyful feast, became pitiful. He fell from the highest position to the lowest. When viewed through God's heart, Jesus was undoubtedly the King of Kings, and even when He fell from the place of glory to establish God's dignity on earth, He did not become disheartened or resentful. Instead, He felt a greater sense of responsibility and was embarrassed before heaven. He felt embarrassed.

When God sent Jesus, He looked forward to a day of glory. The purpose of choosing the people of Israel and laboring for 4,000 years was to send the Messiah and welcome a day of glory. It is unquestionable that God sent Jesus hoping to pioneer an environment of freedom so that all people could sing songs of freedom and liberation to Him. But what kind of path did Jesus take? Although Jesus' position and circumstances fell, He worried about God's will and felt embarrassed before heaven.

He said, "Father, I am ashamed, Father, I am ashamed." Even in a lonely place, He did not weep for Himself.

When thinking of God's labor over 4,000 years, holding onto the nation, and considering the deep sorrow in the Father's heart, He could not think of striking down the nation just because He was persecuted and fell. Why? Because He knew that Israel was a nation established by God through a bond of destiny. Therefore, even while falling, He held onto the people of Israel and prayed.

You must understand that Jesus was such a person. Jesus, who went to pray, was pitiful. He felt embarrassed. God sent Jesus to find a day of freedom, to fulfill His will, and to establish a bond of heart, yet Jesus, being rejected by the nation and entering a lonely mountain to pray, was an embarrassed Jesus. Is that not so?

If Jesus had fulfilled His will, God would have welcomed a day of freedom, and if Jesus had accomplished His purpose, a bond of heart would have been established between God and humanity. Moreover, divine dignity would have been established on earth. And God would have proudly presented Jesus, standing in glory, before Satan, saying, "Look at the character, dignity, and majesty of Jesus." However, you must understand how God's heart felt when He looked at Jesus, who had no content to boast about.

From the day He was rejected by the nation, Jesus made a resolution. When He saw that the chosen people of Israel, whom heaven had labored for 4,000 years, were on the brink of death, Jesus felt the hunger of the nation and voluntarily walked the path of hunger, and when He felt the nakedness of the nation, He voluntarily walked the path of nakedness.

Jesus decided to carry the cross and walk the path of death in the Garden of Gethsemane. Of course, He had such thoughts during His three years of public ministry, but the final decision was made there. What do you think Jesus' heart was like? He felt frustrated. He felt embarrassed. Jesus was a frustrated Jesus. Jesus was an embarrassed Jesus. When He looked to heaven, He felt embarrassed, and when He looked at the world, He felt frustrated. You must understand this.

Jesus came as the King of Kings but never felt the joy of being the King of Kings even for a moment. He could not establish His dignity. We believe in such a Jesus. The Jesus we believe in could not establish His dignity, could not welcome a day of freedom, and could not have a moment of glory, so all of us who believe in Jesus must walk that same path.

To follow Jesus, we must emulate the hungry Jesus. To follow Jesus, we must understand His frustrating circumstances. To follow Jesus, we must have a heart that feels embarrassed before heaven. This is the heart that a believer must have.

What should today's Christian believers possess? It is a heart that feels embarrassed before heaven. And this heart that feels embarrassed before heaven must be able to capture all of one's emotions. Only with such a heart can one stand before Jesus. Furthermore, when facing the earth, one must feel frustrated. A person who lives with frustration toward the earth and embarrassment toward heaven does not have to worry about what they eat, what they wear, or what they are criticized for. If there is a way to resolve this frustrating and embarrassing heart, one must be able to walk the path of death. Have you ever felt this while believing in Jesus?

Look. People have come out with great desires. We have bodies filled with great desires. We have minds. Furthermore, we have hearts. Yet today, among the countless humanity, there are very few who live centered on their hearts. Many live centered on their bodies, but few live centered on their hearts.

Among those who live centered on their bodies, there are also those who feel frustration. Is that not so? The body does not always do what it wants. It is the ordinary person's life to feel pain just to sustain a life with one body. If the ordinary person's life is like this, how much more did Jesus know God's circumstances? He knew God's heart. He knew God's wishes. His body, mind, and heart were one. His body was captured before His heart, and His heart was captured before His feelings, unwavering whether in life or death. His heart was solely one.

Yet when He set out to embrace God's will, the world stood in His way. When He tried to act according to His heart, His body was restricted. Jesus, whose heart, body, and feelings were one, had to live as the subject connecting God's heart to humanity, yet He had to walk a path divided into three: one for His heart, one for His body, and one for God's heart. You must understand Jesus' position.

What did Jesus have to manage in such circumstances? Unable to manage His body, He had to manage the ideology that would allow God to come close and manage His feelings. What had to be done with these? They had to be established on earth. What had to be done next? They had to be reintegrated into the heart. So how great was Jesus' suffering? He was a frustrated Jesus. He was an embarrassed Jesus before the Father, who had labored for 4,000 years.

What kind of environment are you living in today? You know that well. When someone asks you whether you are living centered on your body, centered on your heart, or centered on some ideology, thought, or feeling, what will you answer? You must understand what position you are in. There is pain for those who want to live centered on their body, but for those who decide to live centered on their heart, the suffering is several times greater.

Jesus came with historical feelings, historical circumstances, and historical wishes. And not only did He bring feelings, circumstances, and wishes of the times, but also future feelings...
and circumstances and wishes. The heart, circumstances, and wishes of Jesus not only represent the heart, circumstances, and wishes of humanity but also those of God. Jesus came to fulfill God's wishes and to unite God's heart and circumstances to resolve the heart's grievances.

What does the Bible center around and what is it trying to address? It is a scripture aimed at centering the heart and managing the body. Therefore, it says to strike the body, to strike the body. Thus, we must manage the body, manage the heart, and manage the feelings. The ethics and morals up to today are systems that govern the body. They are not systems that govern the conscience. They serve as an intermediary mission to create a character that can follow the commands of conscience by limiting the actions of the body. This has been the morality until now.

What did Jesus try to manage first when He came to this earth? The hearts and bodies of the Israelite people should have been managed and united before Jesus came. Only then could Jesus come and carry out His role as the Messiah. However, the Israelite people were divided, with the body separate from the heart. Therefore, Jesus could not engage with the Israelite people.

The body, heart, and feelings of Jesus represent heaven. Jesus came to this earth as such a representative. However, this representative did not move the universe with His body but moved it with God's heart. Humans also deepen social connections through affection; how much more so would God, who created humanity, lack heavenly feelings?

God wanted to manifest Jesus as the ultimate model who completed a character with unchanging feelings that could resonate with the unchanging feelings of heaven and the ideological principles of heaven along with the fortunes of heaven and earth. Did Jesus see anyone whom He loved dearly while carrying His heart? He did not. Have you seen such a person?

Mary Magdalene—who, filled with sorrow over the death of her teacher, wandered in darkness seeking Jesus' tomb—sought to hold onto the Jesus she longed for, who appeared to her in glory after His resurrection. However, Jesus told her not to touch Him. It was a heartbreaking statement.

What should believers today understand? It is about who that one person is whom Jesus can truly love, representing the billions of humanity on this earth. That one person is blessed. They are the person whom Jesus can love with one hundred percent of His heart by representing God's heart, the person who can fulfill any ideological world or wish that Jesus longs for. We have not seen such a person, one who can make Jesus rejoice with their heart and body. We have not seen anyone who rejoices with their body either. How did Jesus live? He was a person of tears and sorrow.

Now, what we must pray for while we are alive is: "Lord, knowing that You left with grievances, please send us a son or daughter with whom You can rejoice." We should also hope to be established before all people in a form that can enjoy with God and all things, possessing God's heart one hundred percent. If we cannot become such a self, we should at least have a heart that is grateful to God for seeing such a person. Those who do not even have that heart have no relation to the kingdom of God's glory.

We must pray. We must put in our sincerity. Even if it means sacrificing everything, we must put in our sincerity.

We are called to resolve the grievances of Jesus and God. Although our bodies may be small, our hearts must transcend the universe and pierce through the path of heaven to connect with God's heart. If it cannot be done with the body, we must first receive the heart of Jesus in our hearts and then bring Him back with our bodies. Those who cannot do this will have no connection to the Lord even if He comes again.

What was the last content of Jesus' prayer for His beloved disciples before He was arrested? He said, "Father, just as You and I are one, let them also be one." What does it mean to be one? It means my body is Yours, and my heart is Yours. Furthermore, it means even my feelings are Yours.

Everyone, let us not just think of Jesus collapsing in His body and feel sorrow. Jesus was not only nailed in His body. He was also nailed in His heart. We should feel more sorrow for Jesus, who bled from His heart, than for the Jesus who bled from His body. Moreover, we must understand that the heart of love that desired to live with humanity was also in pain. We must recognize that Jesus was one who felt grievances, was troubled, and was embarrassed.

Today, believers know how to hold onto the cross and can look at the bleeding Jesus and weep, but they do not know the cross of the heart's feelings, the cross of circumstances, or the cross of wishes.

When Jesus was nailed, His heart was also nailed along with His body. What is the cross of the heart? What is the cross of feelings? How unjust and resentful it is that for two thousand years of history, He could not teach humanity about the cross of His heart and the cross of His feelings! He is the one who wanted to speak but could not.

Jesus said, "I still have much to say to you, but you cannot bear it now" (John 16:12), and "I came to cast fire on the earth, and how I wish it were already kindled! I have a baptism to be baptized with, and how distressed I am until it is accomplished" (Luke 12:49-50). Was His distress due to His body being hungry? If so, what does a 40-day fast mean, and what does suffering and persecution mean? You must understand that Jesus walked the path of the cross and the path of suffering because He knew that God was experiencing greater suffering than His own and that God was carrying a greater cross than the one He had to bear.

We have long awaited the Lord of glory. With the idea of a glorious resurrection, we have thought that there would be seven years of great tribulation on earth and a wedding feast of the Lamb in the air, and we have only asked, "Lord, help me." Such believers are like thieves; those who are different from the Lord's heart are all enemies. To meet the returning Lord, we must now have the heart to go beyond the path of suffering that Jesus walked and even be willing to walk a greater path. Jesus prayed in the Garden of Gethsemane, worrying about His path, saying, "Not my will, but Yours be done." He felt embarrassment before praying and felt embarrassment even after praying. We must understand that Jesus felt embarrassed when He saw the crowds opposing Him and rebuking His disciples. From the mission sent by God, He knew that He should not be treated that way, but because He felt He had not fulfilled His responsibilities, He felt He deserved to be whipped.

Today, we are awaiting the Lord of glory. We believe that when the Lord comes, the door of happiness will open, and when the Lord comes, the garden of peace will be built, allowing us to live happily with Him for countless years. However, this is an utterly unreasonable thought. To be able to live with Jesus, we must pass through the cross of the body, the cross of the heart, and the cross of feelings. Is that not so? Jesus, who left behind the cross of the body, taught us to follow the integrity of the cross of the body, and He will return to teach us the integrity of the cross of the heart and the integrity of the cross of feelings. Do you think about receiving glory and blessings when you meet the returning Jesus? That is an utterly unreasonable thought. Just wait and see. Is what is being said here a lie or the truth?

If you want to meet the Lord in glory, if you want to become a figure that is most beloved in the eyes of the Lord, if you want to see the figure that pleases the Lord, you must pass through the cross of the body and understand what the cross of the heart and the cross of feelings are, and become someone who prays for the path that the Lord desires. If you cannot do that, you will not be able to meet the Lord.

Look at this world. Our body symbolizes the earth, our heart symbolizes the air, and our feelings and spirit symbolize heaven. Therefore, when clouds gather in your heart, it is like tears flowing; when clouds gather in the air, it rains. Humanity is a miniature form of heaven and earth. If humanity is a miniature universe, then everything must be contained within humanity. Since humans are a microcosmic entity, our hearts are connected to heaven, and our bodies are connected to the earth. Humanity must center around the heart, and everything in the world must be contained within it. The same goes for thoughts and beliefs.

What did Jesus establish on the foundation of the cross? He established the doctrine of Jesus. With this doctrine of Jesus, we must open the door to the world of the heart. After opening the door to the world of the heart, we must open the door to the world of feelings. Finally, we must build the garden of love as bride and groom.

So, what kind of person can pioneer the door of the heart? A person who believes in the Lord is someone who cannot sleep when they see the persecution of the righteous. When a good person is hungry, poorly dressed, and persecuted, their blood boils. That is how God is. Do you have such a heart?

Before praying in the Garden of Gethsemane, Jesus said to His disciples, "My soul is overwhelmed with sorrow to the point of death." Think about it. When a person dies suddenly, their spirit crosses over to heaven. At the moment of death, when the spirit crosses over, countless saints in heaven are watching. God wants to welcome that spirit, which comes amidst thousands of angels. This is the heart of God that we must understand.

Although they are descendants of the fallen who should die, when one person receives salvation on earth and opens the gates of heaven to enter the garden of life, it is the Father's heart that wants to mobilize all the saints surrounding Him to welcome that one person. You all know the parable of the prodigal son, right? When one dies, angels from heaven surely come. At the same time, Satan also comes. This is not an abstract statement. When one enters a certain realm, they always feel it. The angel, as God's special envoy, seeks good conditions and fights against Satan to bring them to God's side. Satan is like a prosecutor, and the angel is like a defense attorney; if one is led away by Satan, there will be indescribable sorrow in heaven. Jesus knew this.

Why did Jesus feel embarrassed? Think about the path Jesus walked. Why did He feel embarrassed? Jesus knew that for 4,000 years, countless prophets and ancestors had come to this earth, enduring infinite pain and sacrifice to prepare for the coming of the Messiah. He came as the Messiah sent by heaven on that foundation, but He could not resolve the grievances of humanity and had to leave. How embarrassed must He have felt? Consider this. Even as He was dying, He could not lift His face. That is why He is praying in paradise. Even if He were to be seated on the heavenly throne, He cannot bear the embarrassment. He truly is one who qualifies as the Messiah.

Do you think that countless spirits in the spirit world are dancing and playing? No, they are cooperating for the earth. The more errands you send to the spirits while on earth, the more the reward will lead to hell. You will end up in prison.

When Jesus was on earth, as the King of kings, He had an organization that could move countless saints centered around the twelve pearl gates and the twenty-four elders, and He had to establish such an organization on earth as well. Jesus came with such a mission, but did He leave it undone?

The twelve disciples? You know that the names of the disciples are written on the foundation stones of the New Jerusalem, right? (Revelation 21:14) Do you know what kind of people they were? They were people who betrayed Jesus during His lifetime. Because Jesus was not welcomed even by the twelve disciples, He felt embarrassed before God when He went to the other side. Do you understand? Now you know the kind of Jesus who left.

Now that the end has come, the Lord will return. He has established countless Christians on this earth, so He must come with a heart that will not be trampled upon. He must come with a heart that will not be trampled upon by humans. This means that He must come with a heart that will not be trampled upon by humans. What does this mean? These are words that Jesus did not say. Do you not know? Do you know what Jesus' heart was like? Jesus knew, but we did not.

After living for over thirty years, when Jesus bore the cross, His body, heart, and feelings were all nailed. Now He must return to liberate the cross of feelings, the cross of the heart, and even the cross of the body. The one who comes to liberate the cross of feelings, the cross of the heart, and the cross of the body is the returning Lord.

What has Jesus been laboring for over the past two thousand years without being able to come to this earth? It is to resolve the cross of the heart before God. He could not speak of it to the humans on earth, but to convey it to them, would it be done just as it is? Conditions must be set to resolve the cross of feelings. This is a problem that must be resolved in the heavenly world before Jesus comes. Because He must come as the Savior of the body, the Savior of the heart, and the Savior of feelings.

The humans on this earth do not know Jesus' heart and do not know His feelings, and they think that is happiness. Even if Jesus taught them everything, humanity would have had no way to resolve His feelings.

Now the time has come. The end has come. Jesus will come to this earth. Do you think He will appear suddenly in glory? No, He will not come that way. He will not come that way. You will naturally know whether what is being said here is a lie or the truth when you go to the spirit world later. At that time, you will not say that you did not hear such words, will you? He will not come that way. No matter how many times you check, He will not come that way.

How will the returning Lord come? The Jesus who left behind the cross of the body will come to this earth again, carrying the cross of the heart. He will bring back the cross of feelings. Therefore, He will hold onto the descendants of those who betrayed Him on this earth and say, "In the past, your ancestors struggled with the cross of the body, but they did not know the cross of the heart. They did not know the cross of feelings. Since they did not know, they can be forgiven."

The returning Lord will come with a heart, feelings, and circumstances.
O Lord, when we are filled with emotion, we must allow You to respond as You did when Mary Magdalene tried to hold onto the resurrected Jesus, rather than saying, "Do not touch me." Until now, countless people have longed for heaven with their fallen bodies, but none of them have received God's love or His sovereign blessings.

If the Lord comes to this earth now, He will come with a heart that can represent God's heart, God's circumstances, and God's ideals, which have never been revealed in the human world until now. 

What is the source of the frustration and embarrassment deeply buried in the heart of Jesus? It is because of the fallen descendants. It is not because Jesus was inadequate, nor is it because God lacked power. Jesus became a parent who had a wayward child, and the path of the cross is about a parent forgiving the sins of the child. We knew that Jesus suffered in body, but we did not understand His heart.

Our hearts have changed a million times regarding the Lord, and we have loved the Lord while changing a million times. However, the heart that can represent heaven, the heart that Jesus seeks, is one that, once it has made a resolution towards God and Jesus, cannot change despite the countless pains that may come. This standard must be established. We must have a heart that does not change according to the trends of the times but remains steadfast according to the Lord's thoughts. 

To welcome the coming Lord, we must have a heart greater than that of the Israelite people. We must have a heart that surpasses that of Peter, who followed Jesus and, upon meeting the resurrected Jesus, regained his senses and was crucified upside down. We must have a heart that is more than just accepting the frustrations and embarrassments of Jesus. 

We must feel the frustrations and embarrassments of Jesus in this age. So, what is Jesus' frustration? Jesus wanted to embrace the nation and the world within His heart. However, at that time, Jesus was not a wealthy man. He was not a man of power. He was a solitary figure who walked the path of tears.

It was not that He lacked heavenly power. It was not that He lacked heavenly glory. It was not that He lacked heavenly blessings. However, Jesus had to resolve the earthly matters first. This Jesus came to this earth longing for many things. Do you know what He longed for at first? What did He long for with that heart? He longed for a true person. A true person! He sought someone whose body, heart, and spirit would not change even if they were split apart.

Jesus longed desperately for true people and the heavenly kingdom. He longed for people with heart, people with spirit. Moreover, what else did He long for? He longed for a nation. A nation! What else did He long for? He longed for the world. What else did He long for? He longed for the Father. He longed for the Father while simultaneously longing for the Father's nation and the Father's world. You must understand this.

Have you ever felt the need for such a person and searched for them? Have you ever fought for a nation that you believe is such a nation? Have you ever fought for a world that you believe is such a world? 

Today, there are countless people, but no one has fought to find a person, a nation, or a world that can be recognized by heaven, by Jesus, and from the depths of their own hearts. There have been people who fought for a single nation, for a single cause, or for a single ideology, but no one has fought to find the world of heavenly heart, the world of heavenly mind, the world of heavenly body, where all beings wish to connect and long for.

Jesus fought for over 30 years. He left without saying a word, even though He had much to say, knowing that expressing those words would not yield any results. Jesus began His three years of public ministry to find the people He longed for, sharing joys and sorrows, feeding them first if there was food, clothing them first if there was clothing, and giving up His comfortable place to provide a resting place for His disciples. Yet, at the end of those three years, the disciples who betrayed Him were not the people Jesus longed for. 

After His resurrection, Jesus asked Peter three times, "Simon son of John, do you love me more than these?" (John 21:15-17). How pitiful it was! Jesus, who sought to reconnect with the betrayer, must have felt immense sorrow. If there had been people in that era who were better than Peter and more fervent than Peter, Jesus would have been able to find solace. The issue was not that Peter was martyred. The issue was that Jesus, who walked the path of a loser, left with a heart full of sorrow. He could not express what kind of personality he longed for. He could not speak about the kind of nation governed by such personalities. He could not speak about the restored world through the ideology of that nation, nor about the nation governed by God. It is frustrating. It is indeed frustrating. 

You must understand that Jesus, looking at the distant mountains, saw countless humanity moving and saw the countless saints in heaven laboring, watching Him, and He could not lift His head before them. The older He got, the more He could not lift His head, and as time passed, the more He was rejected, the more He could think only of death. Thus, He was in a position where death seemed to be the only relief.

However, that was not the end; He promised to come again. What is He coming to find? He is coming to find the people He longed for in His heart throughout His 30 years of life. He is coming to find the nation He longed for in His heart throughout His life. He is coming to find the world He longed for in His heart throughout His life. He is coming to find the people of that nation, to establish that world.

What position are we in today? What do you long for? Do you have a longing heart? 

"O Father, where are Your beloved sons and daughters?" Are there saints on this earth who forget to eat, forget to clothe themselves, and do not even realize their own downfall while desperately searching for such sons and daughters? If there are no such saints among this people, this nation will perish. If there are no such groups in this world, this world will perish.

Today, as members of the Unification Church, we should be grateful for standing in a position of rejection and isolation. We have no money and no power. We should be grateful for that as well. Jesus was trampled upon in body. We are those who understand the heart, the mind, and the circumstances of Jesus, who carried the cross while being trampled. Even if my body does not know the burden of the heart of Jesus who embraced the cross, my heart knows, and my spirit knows. Therefore, we must long for the heart of a true person for this earth and the heart of a person with spirit, thinking of them even when we see food, and even if our clothing is ragged, we must have the heart of a parent who has a wayward child.

We have understood the heart of Jesus, who did not complain even while walking the path of the cross with a heavy heart. We have understood the circumstances of Jesus. We have understood the fate of Jesus, who had to bear a heart full of embarrassment. We have understood that the precious body had to endure hunger, wear ragged clothes, and later, while wearing a royal robe and carrying the cross without tears, He told the weeping women, "Do not weep for me, but weep for yourselves and for your children."

Now we must open our hearts and prepare our bodies to long for the heart of a true person. We must long for the heart of a person with spirit. We must unite to cross over the path of the cross of hunger and the path of the cross of unjust rejection. In the end, we must become a group that is willing to take on the embarrassment and frustration of Jesus, even if it means crossing over the path of death. We must forget our own situations and, at the summit of the cross, at Golgotha, at Gethsemane, become victorious figures who can replace Jesus, who shed tears of blood while being betrayed by the very people who followed Him. We must become a group that can cry out in front of Jesus, even more than Peter, who betrayed Him.

Dear young men and women who have come from all over, your mission is great. The cry of this one young person here today is not a personal plea. When you are hungry for heaven, the voice that cries out, "Father," while shedding tears at the sight of others eating is more precious than dozens of days of fasting prayer. The voice that cries out for a true person and sheds tears because you cannot find that person is the voice that melts God's heart.

To be a protector of the beloved people of God, we must have a heart like that of a parent, struggling and yearning in spirit, even if it means being called a traitor by others. It does not matter if a certain denomination calls us traitors, if a certain nation calls us traitors, or if a certain teacher calls us traitors. Even while being rejected, if there is a group that can shout that they cannot be traitors in their hearts towards heaven, while searching for the welfare of a single-hearted spirit, their steps will never be in vain.

Now we understand. We have known the desires of the Father, the circumstances of the Father, and the heart of the Father. What is filling your hearts? What has captured your hearts? Even if this body falls, we must have the heart to fight for the will of the Father until we fall. Even if we bleed and fall, as long as the blood of life within this body beats and the pulse of this life flows, we must fall with the conviction that we can raise the flag of the Father's life.

I have nothing, no family or children, and no attachments to the nation or the world. This was the unwavering heart and thought that Jesus had. To Him, there was only the Father. Only the heart of the Father, only the mind of the Father, and only the one true person that the Father desired. Therefore, whenever He looked at the world, all He felt was frustration, and all He had was embarrassment.

Jesus lived in this sinful world and, if there is anything that can relieve that frustration and embarrassment, let us make a resolution. We must clench our fists and pour out our final passion towards the three-thousand-li peninsula. Even if we fall, we must go on calling out, "Father." This is the victorious condition that fallen descendants must possess.

We must pray. We must pray that the frustrated heart of Jesus and the embarrassed heart of Jesus be released from my own self. Jesus was betrayed nationally. He was rejected before the twelve apostles. He was also rejected by the Israelite people. Therefore, the coming Lord must be welcomed by the twelve disciples, welcomed by the second Israel, the Christians, and welcomed by the 2.7 billion people of humanity. If we cannot create the conditions to welcome Him, we must carve out an environment in which we can be welcomed, even if it means fighting until we fall.

To do this, we must gather a group that can pour out their blood and flesh and dedicate their passion. We must seek such a group from this three-thousand-li peninsula. We must reach out to the 2.7 billion people who are asleep and to the countless religious people who are sleeping. Let us not eat a meal just for ourselves, nor wear a piece of clothing just for ourselves, nor live a day just for ourselves. There must be such a group.

We have reasons to suffer. We have more material possessions than Jesus. We are more comfortable than Jesus. We live better than Jesus. Since the Lord's path was such and He was sent with compassion, we, who should be His disciples and children, must have the heart that we cannot eat more than that, cannot wear better clothes than that, and cannot sleep better than that. If we find ourselves in difficult circumstances, we must live with tears while eating, with tears while dressing, and with tears while living. Such a group must become the leaders of the church today.

When we look at Christianity in Korea, we must feel indignant. If our blood has not yet cooled and our hearts have not yet cooled, we must become that group before heaven that is saddened by the absence of such a group.

Even if I lack knowledge and have nothing, I must show a heart of unwavering sincerity before this nation. You must understand that heaven is seeking such a group.

We know that the time is drawing near. We know that the world is struggling at the final crossroads of life and death. Where must we go? The Jesus who has gone before us, who carried the cross and left behind the world of ideals, is now informing us. He tells us to walk the path of the cross, not the path of glory.

Now we must make a solemn resolution. We must prepare our past lives. We must manage our surrounding environment. We must reorganize. Do you have a beloved wife? Make her someone the Lord can embrace and love. Do you have beloved children? Make them children whom the Lord can call to His lap and embrace. Is the place you are living now such a place? No.

Since the Lord who has gone before us went that way, the Lord who is coming will also come with the cross. Today, we must make a solemn resolution. We must arm our hearts and spirits and move towards the place where our bodies fit. We must go to the place where our bodies are frustrated and embarrassed. Therefore, those who go to evangelize in rural areas must first take up a pickaxe. Those who go to evangelize in labor fields must know how to carry burdens first. Those who go before the laborers must stand before them and work harder than they do. Those who go before scholars must learn with more effort than they do and guide them. Such things must happen on this earth for the frustrations of heaven to be relieved, and through this process, the embarrassment of heaven will be relieved. You must understand that you must make a solemn resolution.

You know that your bodies are precious. I do not wish to make you suffer. It is not my intention to make you suffer. It is because I have a responsibility to lay a solid foundation for the nation and the world. Soon, we will...
must move forward, even if it means abandoning everything. Even if it means becoming like a refugee, I must walk this path.  
Make this year a year of maximum achievement.  
At the beginning of this year, I declared before you to do the greatest thing that you will never forget throughout your life. Do you have money in your hands right now? Have you held tens of billions or hundreds of millions of won? In your life's journey, have you ever fought to earn money for your own happiness? Regret it. If you have such money, it should be spent for life, for the heavenly kingdom. Have you clung to luxurious dwellings and fought until now? You must learn to forget such things in order to bring comfort to the people of heaven. We must have this resolute determination.  
If there were times in the past when you ate well, you must now regret it. If there were times when you dressed well, you must regret it. Why? Because you lived better than the Lord. If humanity stands in such a position today, it will become a world of peace. The Prince of Peace is the one who walks this path. Only those who can build peace are such people.  
Now, as we move toward the place where thirty million people are crying out, if there is a place where blood and sweat are shed, I will go there; if there is a place where I am scorned, I will go there. I want to emphasize before you to leave behind a connection that calls out to the Father while shedding tears in such places.  
The person speaking here has walked such a path. Even now, there is a heart that is more sincere than yours. If it is for heaven, I am ready to do anything. I cherish you infinitely. I want to bless you wholeheartedly. I want to go to any place of suffering on your behalf. However, you must understand that there are circumstances and difficulties that prevent me from doing this or that because of heaven.  
The Lord's footsteps are awaited not only by those who dig caves in the mountains and pray, but also by those who cultivate fields and grow potatoes to make a living. The Father also has feelings for such people. Therefore, we must go. We must go. Rather than gathering to celebrate a commemorative day, you must become those who can understand the heart of Jesus, who wanted to weep for the remaining Israel.  
Dear ones, the heart of the person speaking here wants to infinitely justify your dignity. I know that some family members in America have said they would do anything the teacher asks, just to give the order. However, because I cannot give orders before you, I do not wish to give orders before them. If there is a blessing, I want to give it to you, and if there is a heavenly connection, I want to establish it before you; this is the heart of the person born of this nation's blood.  
Our nation has a global mission. During the Korean War, dozens of countries shed blood and sweat for this nation, and we must repay the grace of those who shed blood and fell for this nation with our own blood and sweat. We must understand that we have the responsibility to do so. If there is a heart that thinks and worries about such a mission, we must become those who worry with infinite frustration and infinite shame.  
From today, if the Lord, who was so sorrowful, can spread His arms and dance in an environment of freedom, and if we can welcome such a Lord, what could be lacking? If we can love the One we wanted to love and die for Him, what could be lacking? If we can meet the day when the Lord, who has suffered countless pains, can say a word before heaven in a comfortable place, what could be lacking? We must fight for that. We must lament for that. Everyone must move for that. I ask each of you to make a resolute decision for this purpose.  
<Prayer> *There were times when I lamented being born as a Korean people. I knew that I should stand in the place of a traitor, persecuted on behalf of this pitiful and lonely nation, but there were times when I wanted to look at the nation and resent it. However, every time I looked to heaven, I knew that I had to walk this path, even if I was beaten and suffered, and that is why I have come to this day.  
Today, the world and domestic situation is complicated. It is a time to make judgments on the crossroads of life and death. The world’s fate and heavenly fate weigh on the scale of a heavenly life, and I know that I must be placed in a position where I can lean entirely toward heaven. I earnestly hope and wish for this.  
We have come to understand the heart of Jesus, who was frustrated and ashamed, so we must make a firm resolution to relieve that frustration and shame on behalf of this nation and on behalf of all humanity. May we be entrusted with this responsibility and mission, Father, and may we gain a new determination and resolution through the feelings we have felt today.  
Let each of us make a vow and promise before the Father,  
Tomorrow’s me will be an unchanging form, a rock-solid form. I offer myself as a living sacrifice, so please accept me.  
May we become those who can do this. I earnestly ask, and in all things, I pray in the name of the Lord. Amen. *  
4)  
The Father’s Grievance Against the Enemy  
Matthew 23:1-12, 29-39  
<Prayer> There is a significant temporal gap between this time and the time Jesus lived, but through the words we have just read, let us recall once again the figure of Jesus, who stepped forth with an anxious and resolute heart.  
Father, as I look upon the end of Israel, which You have labored for over four thousand years, how sorrowful, regretful, and painful must the heart of Jesus Christ have been, unable to speak words of praise for that nation and having to speak words of lament instead?  
Father, as Jesus gazed upon the countless people writhing on the brink of death, when faced with ignorant masses who would not listen to His counsel or awaken to His teachings, I know that the heavenly anguish pierced His very being. The more that anguish pierced Him, the more He must have wanted to blame the earth. However, no one on earth knew the heart of Christ, who suppressed and endured this.  
To pave the lonely path, I want to regard the figure of Christ as my brother, as my father, and to become one with Him, to shed tears where He sheds tears, to hunger where He hungers, to be naked where He is naked, to be beaten where He is beaten, and to be in the crowd where He is crowded. We have come to know that not being able to stand in the place of those who are crowded has been a historical regret.  
We have come to understand that the world of the heart transcends historical distances. Therefore, let us now find the foundation of the heart, embrace the figure of Christ, and become friends of the heart who can share His circumstances, knowing how to pray in the Garden of Gethsemane in place of Jesus, and knowing how to run toward Mount Calvary in place of Jesus. If we are such sons and daughters, may we realize that He is a friend of Christ and that we are those who have received the heavenly Son beyond history. I earnestly hope and wish for this, beloved Father.  
Please look upon your sons and daughters gathered here. We have nothing. We have nothing to rely on in this land. This nation is the same, but we are even more so. If there is anything to boast of, it is only the tattered appearance of being beaten, scorned, and wounded for the Lord and for heaven.  
When I think that You want to take hold of such people and stand by our side, it is heartbreaking. There are many proud people and proud nations on this earth, yet You must take care of such foolish people like us, and may we become those who feel deeply for Your situation, Father, I earnestly hope and wish for this.  
Jesus shed countless tears while on this earth, yet no one knew it. He had a heart full of blood and tears, appealing to heaven, yet no one understood. Father, I thank You for leading the unification believers to a pitiful place today. I thank You for uniting them in the midst of hunger. Father, may we be sons and daughters who worry about Your will even while being naked and who worry about You even while being beaten.  
This is Your wish, and it is Your will to establish such a figure before this nation to boast of. Now the time has come to fulfill the mission to establish such a figure, so please do not let us be cowardly before this mission, and do not let us hesitate before this mission. May we leave behind all our passion and sincerity before You and become sons and daughters who can leave results and be remembered in Your heart, Father, I earnestly hope and wish for this.
